      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">
        dwarf planet
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">
        Pluto
       </a>
       has five
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_satellite" title="Natural satellite">
        moons
       </a>
       down to a detection limit of about 1 km in diameter. In order of distance from Pluto, they are
       <a href="/wiki/Charon_(moon)" title="Charon (moon)">
        Charon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Styx_(moon)" title="Styx (moon)">
        Styx
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nix_(moon)" title="Nix (moon)">
        Nix
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kerberos_(moon)" title="Kerberos (moon)">
        Kerberos
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Hydra_(moon)" title="Hydra (moon)">
        Hydra
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Charon, the largest of the five moons, is mutually
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidally_locked" title="Tidally locked">
        tidally locked
       </a>
       with Pluto, and is massive enough that Pluto–Charon is sometimes considered a
       <a href="/wiki/Double_planet" title="Double planet">
        double dwarf planet
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moons_of_Pluto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The innermost and largest moon,
       <a href="/wiki/Charon_(moon)" title="Charon (moon)">
        Charon
       </a>
       , was discovered by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Christy" title="James Christy">
        James Christy
       </a>
       on 22 June 1978, nearly half a century after Pluto was discovered. This led to a substantial revision in estimates of Pluto's size, which had previously assumed that the observed mass and reflected light of the system were all attributable to Pluto alone.
      </p>
      <p>
       Two additional moons were imaged by astronomers of the Pluto Companion Search Team preparing for the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">
         New Horizons
        </a>
       </i>
       mission and working with the
       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">
        Hubble Space Telescope
       </a>
       on 15 May 2005, which received the
       <a href="/wiki/Provisional_designation_in_astronomy" title="Provisional designation in astronomy">
        provisional designations
       </a>
       S/2005 P 1 and S/2005 P 2. The
       <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">
        International Astronomical Union
       </a>
       officially named these moons
       <a href="/wiki/Nix_(moon)" title="Nix (moon)">
        Nix
       </a>
       (or Pluto II, the inner of the two moons, formerly P 2) and
       <a href="/wiki/Hydra_(moon)" title="Hydra (moon)">
        Hydra
       </a>
       (Pluto III, the outer moon, formerly P 1), on 21 June 2006.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IAUC_8723_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IAUC_8723-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Kerberos_(moon)" title="Kerberos (moon)">
        Kerberos
       </a>
       , announced on 20 July 2011, was discovered while searching for Plutonian rings.
       <a href="/wiki/Styx_(moon)" title="Styx (moon)">
        Styx
       </a>
       , announced on 7 July 2012, was discovered while looking for potential hazards for
       <i>
        New Horizons
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA20153-MoonsOfPluto-MergedBodies-20151110.jpg">
          <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="3000" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/PIA20153-MoonsOfPluto-MergedBodies-20151110.jpg/400px-PIA20153-MoonsOfPluto-MergedBodies-20151110.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/PIA20153-MoonsOfPluto-MergedBodies-20151110.jpg/600px-PIA20153-MoonsOfPluto-MergedBodies-20151110.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/PIA20153-MoonsOfPluto-MergedBodies-20151110.jpg/800px-PIA20153-MoonsOfPluto-MergedBodies-20151110.jpg 2x" width="400"/>
         </a>
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA20153-MoonsOfPluto-MergedBodies-20151110.jpg" title="Enlarge">
           </a>
          </div>
          <center>
           Small moons of Pluto - studies suggest the moons were the result of merged bodies.
          </center>
         </div>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Charon">
        Charon
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moons_of_Pluto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Charon">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA19856-PlutoCharon-NewHorizons-Color-20150714.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="501" data-file-width="2526" height="44" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/PIA19856-PlutoCharon-NewHorizons-Color-20150714.jpg/220px-PIA19856-PlutoCharon-NewHorizons-Color-20150714.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/PIA19856-PlutoCharon-NewHorizons-Color-20150714.jpg/330px-PIA19856-PlutoCharon-NewHorizons-Color-20150714.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/PIA19856-PlutoCharon-NewHorizons-Color-20150714.jpg/440px-PIA19856-PlutoCharon-NewHorizons-Color-20150714.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA19856-PlutoCharon-NewHorizons-Color-20150714.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Pluto and Charon, to scale. Photo taken by
         <i>
          New Horizons
         </i>
         on approach.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Charon_(moon)" title="Charon (moon)">
        Charon (moon)
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Charon is about half the diameter of Pluto and is so massive (nearly one eighth of the mass of Pluto) that the system's
       <a href="/wiki/Center_of_mass#Astronomy" title="Center of mass">
        barycenter
       </a>
       lies between them, approximately 960 km above Pluto's surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [a]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Charon and Pluto are also
       <a href="/wiki/Tidal_locking" title="Tidal locking">
        tidally locked
       </a>
       , so that they always present the same face toward each other. The
       <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union#The_XXVIth_General_Assembly_and_the_definition_of_a_planet" title="International Astronomical Union">
        IAU General Assembly
       </a>
       in August 2006 considered a proposal that Pluto and Charon be reclassified as a
       <a href="/wiki/Double_planet" title="Double planet">
        double planet
       </a>
       , but the proposal was abandoned.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Draft_Resolution_5_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Draft_Resolution_5-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Small_moons">
        Small moons
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moons_of_Pluto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Small moons">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Styx_(moon)" title="Styx (moon)">
        Styx (moon)
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nix_(moon)" title="Nix (moon)">
        Nix (moon)
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kerberos_(moon)" title="Kerberos (moon)">
        Kerberos (moon)
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Hydra_(moon)" title="Hydra (moon)">
        Hydra (moon)
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pluto_and_its_satellites_(2005).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="792" data-file-width="868" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Pluto_and_its_satellites_%282005%29.jpg/220px-Pluto_and_its_satellites_%282005%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Pluto_and_its_satellites_%282005%29.jpg/330px-Pluto_and_its_satellites_%282005%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Pluto_and_its_satellites_%282005%29.jpg/440px-Pluto_and_its_satellites_%282005%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pluto_and_its_satellites_(2005).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <i>
          Hubble
         </i>
         discovery image of Nix and Hydra
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pluto_moon_P5_discovery_with_moons%27_orbits.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1578" data-file-width="1546" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Pluto_moon_P5_discovery_with_moons%27_orbits.jpg/220px-Pluto_moon_P5_discovery_with_moons%27_orbits.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Pluto_moon_P5_discovery_with_moons%27_orbits.jpg/330px-Pluto_moon_P5_discovery_with_moons%27_orbits.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Pluto_moon_P5_discovery_with_moons%27_orbits.jpg/440px-Pluto_moon_P5_discovery_with_moons%27_orbits.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pluto_moon_P5_discovery_with_moons%27_orbits.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Discovery image of Styx, overlaid with orbits of the satellite system
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Pluto's four small moons orbit Pluto at two to four times the distance of Charon, ranging from Styx at 42,700 kilometres to Hydra at 64,800 kilometres from the barycenter of the system. They have nearly circular
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_motion" title="Direct motion">
        prograde
       </a>
       orbits in the same orbital plane as Charon.
      </p>
      <p>
       All are much smaller than Charon. Nix and Hydra, the two larger, are roughly 42 and 55 kilometers on their longest axis respectively,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-7">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and Styx and Kerberos are 7 and 12 kilometers respectively.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-styx_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-styx-8">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kerberos_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-kerberos-9">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       All four are irregularly shaped.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">
        Characteristics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moons_of_Pluto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Characteristics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Masses_of_Plutonian_moons.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="943" data-file-width="1139" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Masses_of_Plutonian_moons.png/250px-Masses_of_Plutonian_moons.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Masses_of_Plutonian_moons.png/375px-Masses_of_Plutonian_moons.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Masses_of_Plutonian_moons.png/500px-Masses_of_Plutonian_moons.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Masses_of_Plutonian_moons.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The relative masses of Pluto's moons. Charon dominates the system. Nix and Hydra are barely visible and Styx and Kerberos are invisible at this scale.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pluto-Charon_system-new.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="322" data-file-width="640" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Pluto-Charon_system-new.gif/250px-Pluto-Charon_system-new.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Pluto-Charon_system-new.gif/375px-Pluto-Charon_system-new.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Pluto-Charon_system-new.gif/500px-Pluto-Charon_system-new.gif 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pluto-Charon_system-new.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An oblique schematic view of the Pluto–Charon system showing that Pluto orbits a point outside itself. Also visible is the mutual
         <a href="/wiki/Tidal_locking" title="Tidal locking">
          tidal locking
         </a>
         between the two bodies.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Pluto system is highly compact and largely empty.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sternetal_2005_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Sternetal_2005-10">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Moons could potentially orbit Pluto at up to 53% (or 69%, if retrograde) of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hill_sphere" title="Hill sphere">
        Hill
       </a>
       radius, the stable gravitational zone of Pluto's influence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steffl_2006_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Steffl_2006-11">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For example,
       <a href="/wiki/Psamathe_(moon)" title="Psamathe (moon)">
        Psamathe
       </a>
       orbits
       <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">
        Neptune
       </a>
       at 40% of the Hill radius. In the case of Pluto, only the inner 3% of the region where
       <a href="/wiki/Retrograde_and_prograde_motion" title="Retrograde and prograde motion">
        prograde orbits
       </a>
       would be stable is occupied by satellites,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sternetal_2005_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Sternetal_2005-10">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the region from Styx to Hydra is packed so tightly that there is little room for further moons with stable orbits.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kenyon2015_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kenyon2015-12">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An intense search conducted by
       <i>
        New Horizons
       </i>
       confirmed that no moons larger than 4.5 km in diameter exist at the distances up to 180,000 km from Pluto (for smaller distances, this threshold is still smaller).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stern_2015_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Stern_2015-13">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The orbits of the moons are confirmed to be circular and coplanar, with inclinations differing less than 0.4° and eccentricities less than 0.005.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The discovery of Nix and Hydra suggested that Pluto could have a
       <a href="/wiki/Ring_system" title="Ring system">
        ring system
       </a>
       . Small-body impacts can create debris that can form into a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ring_system_(astronomy)" title="Ring system (astronomy)">
        ring system
       </a>
       . However, data from a deep-optical survey by the
       <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Camera_for_Surveys" title="Advanced Camera for Surveys">
        Advanced Camera for Surveys
       </a>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">
        Hubble Space Telescope
       </a>
       , by occultation studies,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pasachoff_2006_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pasachoff_2006-15">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and later by
       <i>
        New Horizons
       </i>
       , suggest that no ring system is present.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Resonances">
        Resonances
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moons_of_Pluto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Resonances">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Styx, Nix, and Hydra are thought to be in a 3-body
       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_resonance" title="Orbital resonance">
        orbital resonance
       </a>
       with orbital periods in a ratio of 18:22:33; the respective ratio of orbits is 11:9:6.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShowalterHamilton2015_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ShowalterHamilton2015-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Regius_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Regius-17">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The ratios should be exact when
       <a href="/wiki/Apsidal_precession" title="Apsidal precession">
        orbital precession
       </a>
       is taken into account. Hydra and Nix are in a simple 2:3 resonance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-resonance1_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-resonance1-18">
         [b]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShowalterHamilton2015_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ShowalterHamilton2015-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Witze2015_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Witze2015-19">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Styx and Nix are in a 11:9 resonance, while the resonance between Styx and Hydra has a ratio of 11:6.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-resonance2_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-resonance2-20">
         [c]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This means that in a recurring cycle there are 11 orbits of Styx for every 9 of Nix and 6 of Hydra. The ratios of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synodic_period" title="Synodic period">
        synodic periods
       </a>
       are then such that there are 5 Styx–Hydra conjunctions and 3 Nix–Hydra conjunctions for every 2 conjunctions of Styx and Nix.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-resonance3_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-resonance3-21">
         [d]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShowalterHamilton2015_16-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ShowalterHamilton2015-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       If
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \lambda }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi>
              λ
              <!-- λ -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \lambda }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\lambda " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b43d0ea3c9c025af1be9128e62a18fa74bedda2a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.355ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       denotes the
       <a href="/wiki/Mean_longitude" title="Mean longitude">
        mean longitude
       </a>
       and
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \Phi }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi mathvariant="normal">
              Φ
              <!-- Φ -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \Phi }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\Phi " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/aed80a2011a3912b028ba32a52dfa57165455f24" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Libration" title="Libration">
        libration
       </a>
       angle, then the
       <a href="/wiki/Resonant_trans-Neptunian_object#Toward_a_formal_definition" title="Resonant trans-Neptunian object">
        resonance
       </a>
       can be formulated as
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \Phi =3\cdot \lambda _{\rm {Styx}}-5\cdot \lambda _{\rm {Nix}}+2\cdot \lambda _{\rm {Hydra}}=180^{\circ }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

              Φ

             </mi>

              =
             </mo>
             <mn>
              3
             </mn>
             <mo>
              ⋅
              <!-- ⋅ -->
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               λ
               <!-- λ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 S
                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 t
                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 y
                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 x
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo>
              −
              <!-- − -->
             </mo>
             <mn>
              5
             </mn>
             <mo>
              ⋅
              <!-- ⋅ -->
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               λ
               <!-- λ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 N
                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 i
                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 x
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo>
              +
             </mo>
             <mn>
              2
             </mn>
             <mo>
              ⋅
              <!-- ⋅ -->
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               λ
               <!-- λ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 H
                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 y
                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 d
                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">

                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">

                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <msup>
              <mn>
               180
              </mn>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mo>
                ∘
                <!-- ∘ -->
               </mo>
              </mrow>
             </msup>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \Phi =3\cdot \lambda _{\rm {Styx}}-5\cdot \lambda _{\rm {Nix}}+2\cdot \lambda _{\rm {Hydra}}=180^{\circ }}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="{\displaystyle \Phi =3\cdot \lambda _{\rm {Styx}}-5\cdot \lambda _{\rm {Nix}}+2\cdot \lambda _{\rm {Hydra}}=180^{\circ }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/59667eceff79bbe9ef1fe71de2c9d0bc98820155" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:41.713ex; height:3.009ex;"/>
       </span>
       . As with the
       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_resonance#Laplace_resonance" title="Orbital resonance">
        Laplace resonance
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Galilean_moons" title="Galilean moons">
        Galilean satellites
       </a>
       of Jupiter, triple conjunctions never occur.
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \Phi }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mi mathvariant="normal">
              Φ
              <!-- Φ -->
             </mi>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \Phi }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\Phi " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/aed80a2011a3912b028ba32a52dfa57165455f24" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/>
       </span>
       librates about 180° with an amplitude of at least 10°.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShowalterHamilton2015_16-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-ShowalterHamilton2015-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       All of the outer circumbinary moons are also close to mean motion resonance with the Charon–Pluto orbital period. Styx, Nix, Kerberos, and Hydra are in a 1:3:4:5:6 sequence of
       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_resonance#Coincidental_'near'_ratios_of_mean_motion" title="Orbital resonance">
        near resonances
       </a>
       , with Styx approximately 5.4% from its resonance, Nix approximately 2.7%, Kerberos approximately 0.6%, and Hydra approximately 0.3%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matson_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Matson-22">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It may be that these orbits originated as forced resonances when Charon was tidally boosted into its current synchronous orbit, and then released from resonance as Charon's orbital eccentricity was tidally damped. The Pluto–Charon pair creates strong tidal forces, with the gravitational field at the outer moons varying by 15% peak to peak.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       However, it was calculated that a resonance with Charon could boost either Nix or Hydra into its current orbit, but not both: boosting Hydra would have required a near-zero Charonian eccentricity of 0.024, whereas boosting Nix would have required a larger eccentricity of at least 0.05. This suggests that Nix and Hydra were instead captured material, formed around Pluto–Charon, and migrated inward until they were trapped in resonance with Charon.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The existence of Kerberos and Styx may support this idea.
      </p>
      <center>
       <div class="center">
        <div class="noresize thumb tnone" style=";">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="overflow:hidden;width:452px;">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:114px; overflow:hidden; position:relative; background-color:white;">
           <div style=";left:0px; top:0px; width:450px; position:absolute;">
            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hydra,_Nix,_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png" title="Configurations of Hydra (blue), Nix (red) and Styx (black) over one quarter of the cycle of their mutual orbital resonance.              <img alt="" data-file-height="1122" data-file-width="1496" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png/450px-Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png/675px-Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png/900px-Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png 2x" width="450"/>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div style="text-align:left; background-color:transparent; line-height:110%;">
           </div>
           <div style="visibility:hidden">
            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hydra,_Nix,_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png">
             <img alt="" data-file-height="1122" data-file-width="1496" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png/450px-Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png/675px-Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png/900px-Hydra%2C_Nix%2C_Styx_orbital_resonance_cycle.png 2x" width="450"/>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rotation">
        Rotation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moons_of_Pluto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rotation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:300px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:640px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/PIA20052-SmallMoonsOfPluto-Animation-20151110.webm/640px--PIA20052-SmallMoonsOfPluto-Animation-20151110.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:640px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="60.133" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="PIA20052-SmallMoonsOfPluto-Animation-20151110.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/b6/PIA20052-SmallMoonsOfPluto-Animation-20151110.webm/PIA20052-SmallMoonsOfPluto-Animation-20151110.webm.720p.webm" type="video/webm;          <img alt="File:PIA20052-SmallMoonsOfPluto-Animation-20151110.webm" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/PIA20052-SmallMoonsOfPluto-Animation-20151110.webm/300px--PIA20052-SmallMoonsOfPluto-Animation-20151110.webm.jpg" style="width:300px;height:225px"/>

          <span class="play-btn-large">
           <span class="mw-tmh-playtext">
            Play media
           </span>
          </span>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA20052-SmallMoonsOfPluto-Animation-20151110.webm" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <center>
          Rotations of the small moons of Pluto
          <br/>
          (animation; 01:00; released 10 November 2015)
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Nix_(moon)" title="Nix (moon)">
        Nix
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hydra_(moon)" title="Hydra (moon)">
        Hydra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Styx_(moon)" title="Styx (moon)">
        Styx
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Kerberos_(moon)" title="Kerberos (moon)">
        Kerberos
       </a>
       rotate
       <a href="/wiki/Chaos_theory" title="Chaos theory">
        chaotically
       </a>
       . According to Mark R. Showalter,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShowalterHamilton2015_16-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-ShowalterHamilton2015-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       "Nix can flip its entire pole. It could actually be possible to spend a day on Nix in which the sun rises in the east and sets in the north. It is almost random-looking in the way it rotates."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20150603_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20150603-24">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is because they are in a dynamically changing gravitational field caused by Pluto and Charon orbiting each other. The variable gravitational field creates torques that make Nix and Hydra
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tumbling_(rigid_body)" title="Tumbling (rigid body)">
        tumble
       </a>
       . The torques are increased because the moons are elongated and not
       <a href="/wiki/Sphere" title="Sphere">
        spherical
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShowalterHamilton2015_16-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-ShowalterHamilton2015-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa.gov_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nasa.gov-25">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drake_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Drake-27">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Only one other moon,
       <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">
        Saturn
       </a>
       's moon
       <a href="/wiki/Hyperion_(moon)" title="Hyperion (moon)">
        Hyperion
       </a>
       , is known to tumble,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drake_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Drake-27">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       though it is likely that
       <a href="/wiki/Moons_of_Haumea" title="Moons of Haumea">
        Haumea's moons
       </a>
       do so as well.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RapidlyRotating_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-RapidlyRotating-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">
        Origin
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moons_of_Pluto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Origin">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Creation_of_the_moons_of_Pluto.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="990" data-file-width="1502" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Creation_of_the_moons_of_Pluto.jpg/200px-Creation_of_the_moons_of_Pluto.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Creation_of_the_moons_of_Pluto.jpg/300px-Creation_of_the_moons_of_Pluto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Creation_of_the_moons_of_Pluto.jpg/400px-Creation_of_the_moons_of_Pluto.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Creation_of_the_moons_of_Pluto.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Formation of Pluto's moons. 1: a
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kuiper_belt_object" title="Kuiper belt object">
          Kuiper belt object
         </a>
         approaches
         <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">
          Pluto
         </a>
         ; 2: it impacts Pluto; 3: a
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dust_ring" title="Dust ring">
          dust ring
         </a>
         forms around Pluto; 4: the
         <a href="/wiki/Debris" title="Debris">
          debris
         </a>
         aggregates to form Charon; 5: Pluto and
         <a href="/wiki/Charon_(moon)" title="Charon (moon)">
          Charon
         </a>
         relax into spherical bodies.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       It is suspected that Pluto's satellite system was
       <a href="/wiki/Collisional_family" title="Collisional family">
        created by a massive collision
       </a>
       , similar to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giant_impact_hypothesis" title="Giant impact hypothesis">
        "big whack"
       </a>
       thought to have created the
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        Moon
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canup_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Canup-29">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stern_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Stern-30">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In both cases, the high
       <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum" title="Angular momentum">
        angular momenta
       </a>
       of the moons can only be explained by such a scenario. The nearly circular orbits of the smaller moons suggests that they were also formed in this collision, rather than being captured Kuiper Belt objects. This and their near
       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_resonance" title="Orbital resonance">
        orbital resonances
       </a>
       with Charon (see below) suggest that they formed closer to Pluto than they are at present and migrated outward as Charon reached its current orbit. Their grey color is different from that of Pluto, one of the reddest bodies in the Solar System. This is thought to be due to a loss of volatiles during the impact or subsequent coalescence, leaving the surfaces of the moons dominated by water ice. However, such an impact should have created additional debris (more moons), yet no moons or rings were discovered by
       <i>
        New Horizons
       </i>
       , ruling out any more moons of significant size orbiting Pluto.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="List">
        List
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moons_of_Pluto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: List">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Pluto's moons are listed here by orbital period, from shortest to longest. Charon, which is massive enough to have
       <a href="/wiki/Hydrostatic_equilibrium" title="Hydrostatic equilibrium">
        collapsed
       </a>
       into a
       <a href="/wiki/Spheroid" title="Spheroid">
        spheroid
       </a>
       at some point in its history, is highlighted in light purple. Pluto has been added for comparison.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShowalterHamilton2015_16-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-ShowalterHamilton2015-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <p>
       The maximum distance between the centers of Pluto and Charon is 19,571 ± 4 km.
      </p>

        </a>

        </span>

      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mutual_events">
        Mutual events
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moons_of_Pluto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mutual events">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charon_Eclipses_Pluto_on_25_February_1989.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="450" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Charon_Eclipses_Pluto_on_25_February_1989.jpg/200px-Charon_Eclipses_Pluto_on_25_February_1989.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Charon_Eclipses_Pluto_on_25_February_1989.jpg/300px-Charon_Eclipses_Pluto_on_25_February_1989.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Charon_Eclipses_Pluto_on_25_February_1989.jpg/400px-Charon_Eclipses_Pluto_on_25_February_1989.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charon_Eclipses_Pluto_on_25_February_1989.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Simulated view of Charon transiting Pluto on 25 February 1989.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occultations,_transits,_and_eclipses" title="Occultations, transits, and eclipses">
        Transits
       </a>
       occur when one of Pluto's moons passes between Pluto and the Sun. This occurs when one of the satellites'
       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_node" title="Orbital node">
        orbital nodes
       </a>
       (the points where their orbits cross Pluto's
       <a href="/wiki/Ecliptic" title="Ecliptic">
        ecliptic
       </a>
       ) lines up with Pluto and the Sun. This can only occur at two points in Pluto's orbit, coincidently, these points are near Pluto's perihelion and aphelion.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occultations,_transits,_and_eclipses" title="Occultations, transits, and eclipses">
        Occultations
       </a>
       occur when Pluto passes in front of and blocks one of Pluto's satellites.
      </p>
      <p>
       Charon has an angular diameter of 4
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Degree_of_arc" title="Degree of arc">
        degrees of arc
       </a>
       as seen from the surface of Pluto; the Sun appears much smaller, only 39 to 65
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arcsecond" title="Arcsecond">
        arcseconds
       </a>
       . Charon's proximity further ensures that a large proportion of Pluto's surface can experience an eclipse. Because Pluto always presents the same face towards Charon due to tidal locking, only the Charon-facing hemisphere experiences solar eclipses by Charon.
      </p>
      <p>
       The smaller moons can cast shadows elsewhere. The angular diameters of the four smaller moons (as seen from Pluto) are uncertain. Nix's is 3–9 minutes of arc and Hydra's is 2–7 minutes. These are much larger than the Sun's angular diameter, so total solar eclipses are caused by these moons.
      </p>
      <p>
       Eclipses by Styx and Kerberos are more difficult to estimate, as both moons are very irregular, with angular dimensions of 76.9 x 38.5 to 77.8 x 38.9 arcseconds for Styx, and 67.6 x 32.0 to 68.0 x 32.2 for Kerberos. As such, Styx has no annular eclipses, its widest axis being more than 10 arcseconds larger than the Sun at its largest. However, Kerberos, although slightly larger, cannot make total eclipses as its largest minor axis is a mere 32 arcseconds. Eclipses by Kerberos and Styx will entirely consist of partial and hybrid eclipses, with total eclipses being extremely rare.
      </p>
      <p>
       The next period of mutual events due to Charon will begin in October 2103, peak in 2110, and end in January 2117. During this period, solar eclipses will occur once each Plutonian day, with a maximum duration of 90 minutes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Exploration">
        Exploration
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moons_of_Pluto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Exploration">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The Pluto system was visited by the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">
         New Horizons
        </a>
       </i>
       spacecraft in July 2015. Images with resolutions of up to 330 meters per pixel were returned of Nix and up to 1.1 kilometers per pixel of Hydra. Lower-resolution images were returned of Styx and Kerberos.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
